< Review>
This place sucks to get unloaded at. Make sure you confirm your appt time before arrival because I was told by the broker the load delivered at 07:45 am Thursday. Arrived on time and was told that my appt was actually for 5 am so they had to reschedule me for Saturday. I live in Riverside which isn't far so I went home for a couple days however, the same thing happened to two other drivers who were also told by the brokers to deliver at a certain time and they were also late. I know you might be thinking that it's the brokers' fault but we all had different brokers. It's a communication problem between the smart and final lady who schedules the loads with americold. I was able to go home and re deliver Saturday but the other two drivers sat here overnight and both of them woke up this morning with parking tickets from the city for $160 each. They do Unload fast which is nice though but make sure you confirm your appt time with them a few days in advance otherwise you might be stuck.</Review>

After 5 days at Heavenly Pet Resort, my dog picked up ear mites, and one of her paws had such a deep gash that she had to undergo surgery.

When I picked her up, not only did no one tell me how she'd been, but HER INJURY WAS NOT MENTIONED. WHATSOEVER. We were just rushed out. I had called on Day 3 to extend for a few more days and to inquire about how my baby was doing, and was told that she was good.

So, fast forward to a day or so after the ordeal- I called Gloria (the owner) to express my dissatisfaction and to get an apology and/or refund, at least. I mean, cmon.. I paid $180 to get my dog traumatized, sick, and in pain at this so called "Heavenly" Pet "Resort."

Gloria's response was to laugh it off and sarcastically say, and I quote, "Well what did you expect when you dropped her off here?"

Um, let's see. I expected that my dog would be treated with kindness by the staff. I expected that if she were hurt, she'd be treated.. Ya know, since the paperwork I filled out when I dropped her off specifically said that. I expected that she would probably have a good time, but that, at the least, she would be no worse for the wear. And guess what..  None of that happened.

At the time, I was a disabled 16 year old girl whose living situation was crumbling. If not for being able to leave my furbaby at a kennel for the week, she would have had to be surrendered to a shelter. I felt very taken advantage of by Gloria/this facility. Given my age, my overwhelming personal situation, and the fact that I'd paid with cash, this has been put on the backburner since I didn't have the tools to properly go after this hatefilled woman and her nasty "resort."

So, for now, my goal is to stop anyone else from trusting their animal(s) with these people. PLEASE DO NOT TAKE YOUR ANIMAL TO "HEAVENLY PET RESORT"!!<//review><Pictures>None<//Pictures><Resp>None< /Resp><Gmap_id>0x80c3310d22f4d6f3:0x14846645128304d6</Gmap_id></record>

<Rate>5</Rate>< Review>
The engine blew out on my car a while ago. Never got an official reason but suspect it was the oil pump because the oil light came on before it seized. I had a new engine put in at the shop I normally go to but the transmission had a leak afterwards. I took it back a couple times and they didn't do much to fix it. With time the leak got worse and the transmission started making a whining noise. I took it to Aamco to get fixed, and they were super professional about keeping me updated and contacting me before doing any work. Turns out the original shop had hooked a line up from the brake booster to the transmission dipstick to create pressure and keep it from leaking, but instead the extra pressure blew out the pump seal and a few other parts. Aamco got everything fixed and documented what they found in the transmission.</Review>

<Resp>{'time': 1520450739798, 'text': "Working with extended warranty companies can be confusing and frustrating for the customer. I thought it would be helpful to explain the process....When you have a problem with your vehicle, as this customer has, the first step is to find out if the warranty company will cover the repair. On this customer's vehicle, he had a shifting issue. We offer our initial inspection on the transmission at no charge. Our initial inspection is to test drive the vehicle, check transmission fluid and scan it. After our initial inspection, we felt it necessary to recommend a pan drop. A pan drop helps to see what is happening inside the transmission. In order to do this step, we have to contact the warranty company. Typically, as in this case, the warranty company wants the customer of the vehicle to authorize any additional diagnosis. They want the customer to take some responsibility in the early steps of the process so that, if we are wrong in our dignosis, the customer has to pay for the diagnostic. Once authorized by the customer, if there is a transmission problem, then the warranty company covers the complete repair, including the diagnostic, less the customer's deductible (based on each individual contract). When we dropped the pan on this vehicle, there was metal throughout. This tells us that the transmission is failing. After contacting the warranty company with our findings, they send their own inspector to review the transmission and make a report. The Inspector has 72 hours to come to the center and review the vehicle. The good news is the Inspector's report confirmed our findings. The warranty company searches for a unit or gives the customer an allowance to use towards the repair of their choice. In this case, rather than using the allotted amount to put towards the repair and getting the job done quicker, the customer elected to use the warranty company's supplied unit which took about 10 days and is out of our control. Once the unit was installed and test driven, there was still a drivability problem. This may have been the original cause of the transmission failure. Unfortunately, extended warranty companies take each problem as a separate issue. They told us that the customer would have to authorize additional diagnostic for us to keep going which in this case, was declined. As a courtesy to Mr. Rogers, the Manager reviewed his 30+ page contract in detail, but could not find anything in the contract that would cover the engine problem. He decided to bring it back for further testing and we decided to not charge him an additional diagnostic fee. We found that he was having a misfire issue. On his authorization, we pulled a spark plug and noted that they were completely worn down. They were the wrong spark plugs for his vehicle. Mr. Rogers acknowledged that he wasn't getting that good of gas mileage. When spark plugs are worn to this point, they can send raw fuel through the exhaust and damage the catalytic converters. He authorized us to replace the spark plugs with Motorcraft OEM plugs, but we told him that we could not guarantee this would fix his issue. After replacing the plugs, we testdrove again. It still had a drivability problem. At this point, we recommended that he have his catalytic converters tested at an exhaust shop as we do not perform this type of work. Fortunately, the warranty company acknowledged the transmission damage and covered it even if the cause of the transmission damage is something they do not cover."}<//Resp>< UserId.>
105707620005184197831</UserId.>

< review>
This pho eatery is in the middle of Little Saigon so weekends during peak hours like mornings and lunch will be challenging to navigate and find parking. Weekday mornings is the best time to go with no crowds and no traffic. I ordered the pho tai (rare beef) and the broth was good but they serve clumpy noodles which is a very big pet peeve of mind. Listen pho restaurateurs, clumpy noodles should be banned. Breaking up clumpy noodles with chopsticks in BOTH hands in my piping hot bowl of pho makes me extremely agitated. I will always knock a star off for clumpy noodles. Noodles should always be swimming freely in the soup. Its possible that they have fresh noodles so ask when ordering. What I do like is that their plate of garnishments: Thai basil, culantro (saw-leaf), flash boiled sprouts, jalapenos, lime, and rice paddy herb!  Very few pho shops provide rice paddy herb (citrusy-cumin like flavor) so toss this guy in your bowl to change things up.</review>

<user_id>115511397084962567784<//user_id>< name>
Scott Templeton< /name>
<time>1555199694001< /time><rate>5</rate>< Review>
This is probably my favorite bar in SD. It's always fun, with a great crowd of welcoming locals and a friendly staff.

They have tons of great games, like ping pong, real darts, basketball, pool, a full sized shuffle board, and Foosball. Bring your A game for ping pong or you will get destroyed! The players here are pretty great. They will beat you with a friendly smile though.

I wish they had a better draft selection but they mostly make up for it with their bottle offerings. It seems like they've stepped up their wine selection lately which is great, especially considering they don't serve hard alcohol.

A final note: they have a juke box with a huge selection, so you never know what genre your gonna hear unless you choose what to play. I appreciate the randomness this adds to the ambiance, but some people might find it jarring to go from the Beatles to Dr. Dre to Metallica to Michael Jackson.</Review>

< Text>
What I like about the Triple Crown is the activities provided. You can sit and and watch the world go by with its open front, watch a game or play some pool, darts, ping pong, shuffle board and fooseball.

They do offer food (mostly hamburgers and chips) which helps with the drinking. The beer selections is also decent ranging from cheap Bud to better craft beers (local and not).

This is a great place to hang out with a few friends while keeping everyone entertained.< /Text>

< review>
give me beer, games, and the flattery of being hit on by a couple of swingers and i call this a winner in my book.

we came to triple crown on a lazy weekend afternoon. i love bars that have other forms of entertainment than the standard drunk people watching, and this place has it ALL: shuffleboard, table tennis, darts, pool, foosball...so much fun to be had. there are two table tennis sets (outside patio across from darts boards, and inside 2nd room where the pool tables are). thats where you found me. did i win?? debatable. i get a little too crazy sometimes and the kind gentleman at the pool table had to help us out. which is why i was stoked when the outside neighboring table freed up as its more self contained. but then the darts players had to help out...

and thats where the swingery came into play. i dont think ive ever been summoned via "hey pretty lady" by a female before. well hello there :') and then the dude came over and started playing ping pong with me when my friend went to the bathroom. there was all sorts of cruising going on. so my question is -- is that a regular thing at triple crown? is that where the TRIPLE comes into play?? O_o

They also grill food up outside on the patio...didnt partake but it smelled delicious!< /review>
